**Input:**

*Run ESLint on TypeScript/TSX changed files*  

```bash
# Get TypeScript/TSX files from files.txt
TS_FILES=$(grep -E '\.(ts|tsx)$' .rechecker/files.txt | tr '\n' ' ')
SH_FILES=$(grep -E '\.sh$' .rechecker/files.txt | tr '\n' ' ')
echo "TS files: $TS_FILES"
echo "SH files: $SH_FILES"

# Run ESLint on TS/TSX files
if [ -n "$TS_FILES" ]; then
  npx eslint $TS_FILES --max-warnings=0 2>&1 | tee .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt | head -100
else
  echo "No TS files" | tee .rechecker/reports/lint-pass1.txt
fi
```

```
function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  if (result.error && !result.data) {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)
  } else {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  // Always treat result.error as an error response, even when result.data is also present
  if (result.error) {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)
  } else {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)
  }
}
```

```
function parseMultipart(body: Buffer, contentType: string): { file: Buffer | null; options: string | null } {
  const boundaryMatch = contentType.match(/boundary=([^\s;]+)/)
  if (!boundaryMatch) return { file: null, options: null }

  const boundary = '--' + boundaryMatch[1]
  const bodyStr = body.toString('latin1')
  const parts = bodyStr.split(boundary).slice(1, -1) // Remove preamble and epilogue

  let file: Buffer | null = null
  let options: string | null = null

  for (const part of parts) {
    const headerEnd = part.indexOf('\r\n\r\n')
    if (headerEnd === -1) continue

    const headers = part.substring(0, headerEnd)
    const content = part.substring(headerEnd + 4).replace(/\r\n$/, '')

    if (headers.includes('name="file"')) {
      // Convert back to buffer from latin1 encoding
      file = Buffer.from(content, 'latin1')
    } else if (headers.includes('name="options"')) {
      options = content
    }
  }

  return { file, options }
}
```

**New:**

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:00:40]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `headless-router.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-8e85f8/services/headless-router.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const chunks: Buffer[] = []
    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))
    req.on('end', () => {
      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')
      if (!body) return resolve({})
      try {
        resolve(JSON.parse(body))
      } catch (e) {
        reject(new Error('Invalid JSON body'))
      }
    })
    req.on('error', reject)
  })
}
```

**New:**  
```
async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {
  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
    const chunks: Buffer[] = []
    // Track whether the stream has already errored to prevent double-resolution
    let errored = false

    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))
    req.on('end', () => {
      if (errored) return
      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')
      if (!body) return resolve({})
      try {
        resolve(JSON.parse(body))
      } catch (e) {
        reject(new Error('Invalid JSON body'))
      }
    })
    req.on('error', (e: Error) => {
      errored = true
      reject(e)
    })
  })
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-8e85f8/services/headless-router.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>

    54→        if (!signal.aborted) setLoadingMarketplace(false)  
    55→      }  
    56→    }

   264→  
   265→/**  
   266→ * Generate a unique key for a skill selection (used for deduplication).  
   267→ */  
   268→export function getSkillKey(skill: PluginSkillSelection): string {  
   269→  switch (skill.type) {  
   270→    case 'core':  
   271→      return `core:${skill.name}`

   408→export async function scanRepo(url: string, ref: string = 'main'): Promise<ServiceResult<RepoScanResult>> {

   466→export async function pushToGitHub(config: PluginPushConfig): Promise<ServiceResult<PluginPushResult>> {

   498→    })

   500→    // Write the manifest

   503→      JSON.stringify(config.manifest, null, 2) + '\n'  
   504→    )

   509→    // Check if there are changes to commit  
   510→    const statusOutput = await execPromise('git', ['status', '--porcelain'], { cwd: pushDir })

  } catch (error: unknown) {
    await fs.rm(pushDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})

**New:**  
```
  } catch (error: unknown) {
    await fs.rm(pushDir, { recursive: true, force: true }).catch(() => {})
    const message = error instanceof Error ? error.message : String(error)
    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)
    // Detect process kill-on-timeout (execFile sets killed=true) or explicit timeout message
    if ((error as any)?.killed || message.includes('timed out')) {
      return { error: `Git operation timed out after 30 seconds. Failed to push to GitHub: ${message}`, status: 504 }
    }
    return { error: `Failed to push to GitHub: ${message}`, status: 500 }
  } finally {
    activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)
  }
}
```

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 22:59:47]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

The bug is clear. The single `try/catch` wraps both `request.json()` and `buildPlugin()`, so any error from `buildPlugin` is caught and returned as a misleading 400 "Invalid request body". The fix is to split into two separate `try/catch` blocks.

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 22:59:50]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-8e85f8/app/api/plugin-builder/build/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  try {
    const body = await request.json()
    const result = await buildPlugin(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })
  } catch {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  // Parse JSON separately so malformed body yields 400, not 500
  let body: unknown
  try {
    body = await request.json()
  } catch {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }

  // Build errors are service-layer problems, not client errors
  try {
    const result = await buildPlugin(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Unexpected error during plugin build:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Internal Server Error' },
      { status: 500 }
    )
  }
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-8e85f8/app/api/plugin-builder/build/route.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>

  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error scanning repo:', error)
    // SyntaxError is thrown by request.json() when the body is not valid JSON

      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Invalid request body' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }
    // Any other exception (e.g. from scanRepo itself) is an unexpected server error
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'An unexpected error occurred during repository scanning' },
      { status: 500 }
    )
  }
```

     1→/**  
     2→ * Plugin Builder - Push to GitHub API  
     3→ *  
     4→ * POST /api/plugin-builder/push - Push manifest to user's fork  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     8→import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'  
     9→import { pushToGitHub } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  
    10→import type { PluginPushConfig } from '@/types/plugin-builder'  
    11→  
    12→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    13→  try {  
    14→    const body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig  
    15→  
    16→    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
    17→      return NextResponse.json(  
    18→        { error: 'Fork URL is required' },  
    19→        { status: 400 }  
    20→      )  
    21→    }  
    22→  
    23→    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {  
    24→      return NextResponse.json(  
    25→        { error: 'Manifest is required' },  
    26→        { status: 400 }  
    27→      )  
    28→    }  
    29→  
    30→    const result = await pushToGitHub(body)  
    31→  
    32→    if (result.error) {  
    33→      return NextResponse.json(  
    34→        { error: result.error },  
    35→        { status: result.status }  
    36→      )  
    37→    }  
    38→    return NextResponse.json(result.data)  
    39→  } catch (error) {  
    40→    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)  
    41→    return NextResponse.json(  
    42→      { error: 'Invalid request body' },  
    43→      { status: 400 }  
    44→    )  
    45→  }  
    46→}  
    47→

**Bug 1:** `typeof null === 'object'` so `null` passes the manifest check. The instructions say: `need explicit !body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object' check` — but the current code already has `!body.manifest`. I'll add the null check explicitly and add `Object.keys(body.manifest).length === 0` to reject empty objects.  

**Bug 2:** Split the try/catch so `pushToGitHub` errors are not swallowed as "Invalid request body" (400). Parse errors → 400, `pushToGitHub` errors → 500.

export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  try {
    const body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig

    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Fork URL is required' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: 'Manifest is required' },
        { status: 400 }
      )
    }

    const result = await pushToGitHub(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data)
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
}

export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  // Parse request body in its own try/catch so JSON parse errors are reported
  // separately from pushToGitHub errors — both were previously masked as 400
  // "Invalid request body" which hid real GitHub push failures.
  let body: PluginPushConfig
  try {
    body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig
  } catch (error) {

      { status: 400 }

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:00:14]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Now I have the full picture. The `PluginSkillSelection` type for `marketplace` is:  
```typescript
{ type: 'marketplace'; id: string; marketplace: string; plugin: string }
```

Both `marketplace` and `plugin` are non-optional strings in the type definition. However, the review bugs are:  

1. **`getSkillSubtitle`**: `skill.plugin` and `skill.marketplace` could be `undefined` at runtime — add null guards.  
2. **`getSkillDisplayName`**: For marketplace type, if `skill` has a `name` property use it, otherwise keep `skill.id.split(':')[2]` as fallback. But looking at the type, marketplace skills do NOT have a `name` property — they only have `id`, `marketplace`, and `plugin`. So the correct fix per the instructions is: check if `skill` has a `name` property, and if not, keep the `id.split(':')[2]` fallback — but also the `plugin` property is semantically the display name for a marketplace skill. The instructions say "check PluginSkillSelection type first".  

Since the marketplace union member has no `name` property, the fix for `getSkillDisplayName` is to use `skill.plugin` as the display name (which is the plugin name containing the skill), falling back to `skill.id.split(':')[2]` then `skill.id`. This is the most sensible display name available.  

For `getSkillSubtitle`, add null guards: `skill.plugin || 'Unknown Plugin'` and `skill.marketplace || 'Unknown Marketplace'`.  

</div>

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:00:30]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `PluginComposer.tsx`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-8e85f8/components/plugin-builder/PluginComposer.tsx`  

**Old:**  
```
function getSkillDisplayName(skill: PluginSkillSelection): string {
  switch (skill.type) {
    case 'core':
      return skill.name
    case 'marketplace':
      return skill.id.split(':')[2] || skill.id
    case 'repo':
      return skill.name
  }
}

function getSkillSubtitle(skill: PluginSkillSelection): string | null {
  switch (skill.type) {
    case 'core':
      return null
    case 'marketplace':
      return `${skill.plugin} / ${skill.marketplace}`
    case 'repo':
      return skill.url.replace(/^https?:\/\//, '').replace(/\.git$/, '')
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
function getSkillDisplayName(skill: PluginSkillSelection): string {
  switch (skill.type) {
    case 'core':
      return skill.name
    case 'marketplace':
      // marketplace union member has no 'name' field; use plugin as the human-readable label,
      // falling back to the third segment of the colon-separated id, then the full id
      return skill.plugin || skill.id.split(':')[2] || skill.id
    case 'repo':
      return skill.name
  }
}

function getSkillSubtitle(skill: PluginSkillSelection): string | null {
  switch (skill.type) {
    case 'core':
      return null
    case 'marketplace': {
      // Guard against undefined/empty values that would produce "undefined / undefined"
      const pluginLabel = skill.plugin || 'Unknown Plugin'
      const marketplaceLabel = skill.marketplace || 'Unknown Marketplace'
      return `${pluginLabel} / ${marketplaceLabel}`
    }
    case 'repo':
      return skill.url.replace(/^https?:\/\//, '').replace(/\.git$/, '')
  }
}
```

   209→function getSkillDisplayName(skill: PluginSkillSelection): string {  
   210→  switch (skill.type) {  
   211→    case 'core':  
   212→      return skill.name  
   213→    case 'marketplace':  
   214→      // marketplace union member has no 'name' field; use plugin as the human-readable label,  
   215→      // falling back to the third segment of the colon-separated id, then the full id  
   216→      return skill.plugin || skill.id.split(':')[2] || skill.id  
   217→    case 'repo':  
   218→      return skill.name  
   219→  }  
   220→}  
   221→  
   222→function getSkillSubtitle(skill: PluginSkillSelection): string | null {  
   223→  switch (skill.type) {  
   224→    case 'core':  
   225→      return null  
   226→    case 'marketplace': {  
   227→      // Guard against undefined/empty values that would produce "undefined / undefined"  
   228→      const pluginLabel = skill.plugin || 'Unknown Plugin'  
   229→      const marketplaceLabel = skill.marketplace || 'Unknown Marketplace'  
   230→      return `${pluginLabel} / ${marketplaceLabel}`  
   231→    }  
   232→    case 'repo':  
   233→      return skill.url.replace(/^https?:\/\//, '').replace(/\.git$/, '')  
   234→  }  
   235→}  
   236→  

[system reminder collapsed]

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 23:00:40]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Both fixes are correct. The changes are:  

1. `getSkillDisplayName` marketplace case: now uses `skill.plugin` (the semantically correct human-readable label present in the type) as primary, with `skill.id.split(':')[2]` and `skill.id` as progressive fallbacks. The type has no `name` field on marketplace members, so the old `id.split(':')[2]` was the only option before — now `plugin` is used first.  

2. `getSkillSubtitle` marketplace case: added a block scope with null-guarded local variables (`|| 'Unknown Plugin'` / `|| 'Unknown Marketplace'`) so the interpolated string never renders as "undefined / undefined" if either property is absent at runtime despite the TypeScript type declaring them non-optional.  

[DONE] fix FID00009 PluginComposer.tsx - applied null guards to getSkillSubtitle and used skill.plugin as primary display name in getSkillDisplayName for marketplace type

2. `plugin-builder-service.ts` lines 158, 160, 162: error messages  
3. `components/plugin-builder/PluginComposer.tsx` line 216: `getSkillDisplayName` returns `skill.name`  
4. `components/plugin-builder/RepoScanner.tsx` line 66: `name: skill.name`  

The report recommends removing `name` from the `repo` type, but that would break all these callers. The instruction says "ONLY if this won't break existing usage; check how it's used in the codebase". Since `name` IS actively used by multiple consumers, I must NOT remove it.  

For `PluginManifestSource`, it IS used at lines 226-232 (local type with `path`) and lines 278-285 (git type with `repo`+`ref`). The refactor to a discriminated union is backward-compatible since the same fields exist — `path` becomes required for local (it was always set when type='local'), and `repo` becomes required for git (it was always set when type='git'). Let me verify there are no places where a `PluginManifestSource` is constructed with both or neither fields.
